   <h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" lang="en">Education Index</h1> 
   <div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content"> 
    <div id="siteSub" class="noprint">
     From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia
    </div> 
    <div id="contentSub"></div> 
    <div id="contentSub2"></div> 
    <div id="jump-to-nav"></div> <a class="mw-jump-link" href="#mw-head">Jump to navigation</a> <a class="mw-jump-link" href="#searchInput">Jump to search</a>

     <div class="mw-parser-output">
      <div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">
       Component of the Human Development Index
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:402px;">

       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>An <b>Education index</b> is found as a component of the <a href="/wiki/Human_Development_Index" title="Human Development Index">Human Development Index</a> published every year by the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a>, with the <a href="/wiki/GDP" class="mw-redirect" title="GDP">GDP Index</a> and <a href="/wiki/Life_Expectancy_Index" class="mw-redirect" title="Life Expectancy Index">Life Expectancy Index</a>, to measure the <a href="/wiki/Educational_attainment" title="Educational attainment">educational attainment</a>, <a href="/wiki/GDP_per_capita" class="mw-redirect" title="GDP per capita">GDP per capita</a> and <a href="/wiki/Life_expectancy" title="Life expectancy">life expectancy</a>. </p>
      <p>Since 2010, the Education Index has been measured by combining average adult years of schooling with expected years of schooling for children, each receiving 50% weighting. Before 2010, the Education Index was measured by the adult <a href="/wiki/Literacy" title="Literacy">literacy</a> rate (with two-thirds weighting) and the combined primary, secondary, and tertiary <a href="/wiki/Gross_enrollment_ratio" class="mw-redirect" title="Gross enrollment ratio">gross enrollment ratio</a> (with one-third weighting). The adult literacy rate gives an indication of the ability to read and write, while the GER gives an indication of the level of education from <a href="/wiki/Kindergarten" title="Kindergarten">kindergarten</a> to <a href="/wiki/Postgraduate_education" title="Postgraduate education">postgraduate education</a>. </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Education" title="Education">Education</a> is a major component of <a href="/wiki/Quality_of_life" title="Quality of life">well-being</a> and is used in the measure of <a href="/wiki/Economic_development" title="Economic development">economic development</a> and <a href="/wiki/Quality_of_life" title="Quality of life">quality of life</a>, which is a key factor determining whether a country is a <a href="/wiki/Developed_country" title="Developed country">developed</a>, <a href="/wiki/Developing_country" title="Developing country">developing</a>, or <a href="/wiki/Least_Developed_Country" class="mw-redirect" title="Least Developed Country">underdeveloped</a> country. </p> 
      <div id="toc" class="toc" role="navigation" aria-labelledby="mw-toc-heading">

        <dl>
         <dd>
          Mean years of schooling <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
            <math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" alttext="{\displaystyle ({\textrm {MYS}})}"> <semantics> 
              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD"> 
               <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0"> 
                <mo stretchy="false">
                 (
                </mo> 
                <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD"> 
                 <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD"> 
                  <mtext>
                   MYS
                  </mtext> 
                 </mrow> 
                </mrow> 
                <mo stretchy="false">
                 )
                </mo> 
               </mstyle> 
              </mrow> 
              <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">
               {\displaystyle ({\textrm {MYS}})}
              </annotation> 
             </semantics> 
            </math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/b326dc0c7246c5265ae18f37afc4535e5dc61917" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:6.976ex; height:2.843ex;" alt="{\displaystyle ({\textrm {MYS}})}"></span> is a calculation of the average number of years of education received by people ages 25 and older in their lifetime based on education attainment levels of the population converted into years of schooling based on theoretical duration of each level of education attended.<sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup>
         </dd> 
         <dd>
          Fifteen is the projected maximum of this indicator for 2025.
         </dd>
        </dl> 
        <ul>
         <li>Expected Years of Schooling Index: <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
            <math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" alttext="{\displaystyle EYSI={\frac {\textrm {EYS}}{18}}}"> <semantics> 
              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">

                  </mn>

        </ul> 
        <dl>
         <dd>
          Expected Years of Schooling <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
            <math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" alttext="{\displaystyle ({\textrm {EYS}})}"> <semantics> 
              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD"> 
               <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0"> 
                <mo stretchy="false">
                 (
                </mo> 
                <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD"> 
                 <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD"> 
                  <mtext>
                   EYS
                  </mtext> 
                 </mrow> 
                </mrow> 
                <mo stretchy="false">
                 )
                </mo> 
               </mstyle> 
              </mrow> 
              <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">
               {\displaystyle ({\textrm {EYS}})}
              </annotation> 
             </semantics> 
            </math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/710247fb0721eaa31929a68ac30b60767f23f2a6" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:6.428ex; height:2.843ex;" alt="{\displaystyle ({\textrm {EYS}})}"></span> is a calculation of the number of years a child is expected to attend school, or university, including the years spent on repetition. It is the sum of the age-specific enrollment ratios for primary, secondary, post-secondary non-tertiary and tertiary education and is calculated assuming the prevailing patterns of age-specific enrollment rates were to stay the same throughout the child's life. Expected years of schooling is capped at 18 years.<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup>
         </dd> 
         <dd>
          Eighteen is equivalent to achieving a master's degree in most countries.
         </dd>
        </dl>
       </dd>
      </dl> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="2015">2015</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Education_Index&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: 2015">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="2007">2007</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Education_Index&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: 2007">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <p>Change in value from the last report is given as follows: </p> 
      <ul>
       <li><img alt="Increase" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Increase2.svg/11px-Increase2.svg.png" decoding="async" title="Increase" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Increase2.svg/17px-Increase2.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Increase2.svg/22px-Increase2.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="300" data-file-height="300"> = increase.</li> 
       <li><img alt="Steady" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Steady2.svg/11px-Steady2.svg.png" decoding="async" title="Steady" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Steady2.svg/17px-Steady2.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Steady2.svg/22px-Steady2.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="300" data-file-height="300"> = steady.</li> 
       <li><img alt="Decrease" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Decrease2.svg/11px-Decrease2.svg.png" decoding="async" title="Decrease" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Decrease2.svg/17px-Decrease2.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Decrease2.svg/22px-Decrease2.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="300" data-file-height="300"> = decrease.</li>
      </ul> 
      <p>The latest index was released in the Human Development Report 2009 on October 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup> This statistical update covers the period up to 2007: 1 is the highest possible theoretical score, indicating perfect education attainment. </p>
      <p>All countries considered to be <a href="/wiki/Developed_countries" class="mw-redirect" title="Developed countries">developed countries</a> possess a minimum score of 0.8 or above, although the great majority have a score of 0.9 or above. For ranking based on the <a href="/wiki/Human_Development_Index" title="Human Development Index">Human Development Index</a>, see <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_Human_Development_Index" title="List of countries by Human Development Index">List of countries by Human Development Index</a>. </p>
